< Review>
The food is really quite good, but the service is hit or miss. This isn't the place if you have somewhere to be and need a quick bite. I stayed at the Four Points Sheraton and had breakfast here three times - the buffet, decent; the bacon/eggs/breakfast potatoes/toast breakfast, very good & a large portion; and the pancakes/eggs/bacon breakfast, also very good & a large portion. Their quinoa bowl w/a fried egg on top is very tasty as a healthy option and their mesquite chicken sandwich is delicious. The prices are reasonable for what you get, unless you want cereal that is - $6.50 seems a bit steep.<//Review>

Just my first experience here for a contact exam. Easy to make an appointment, and the front office staff was great. I was seen as soon as I arrived for my appointment, and whisked back into their state of the art room with all the check-in gear (e.g. the puff of air machine). Here, they even had one I hadn't seen before, which flashed a bright light and took a pic of the inside of your eye. I was seen by the doctor next. Doctor was professional and clearly explained procedures as he went. When he got to the eye exam, he mentioned that he could review the pictures of the inside of my eye (taken by the machine at the beginning), it's not fully covered by insurance, would cost $39 out of pocket, most people do it. I hesitated - when I thought about it, I realized it was the same as dilation, so I asked about out of pocket cost for that. He then told me yes, it's an option, and that was covered. I felt a bit upsold here, and like the office wasn't expecting me to choose dilation. Cool tech, but for me the money saved was worth the inconvenience. Doctor asked if I drove myself, and advised caution driving home. He administered the dilation drops, and let me wait in the exam room for the 20 min for them to take effect, which I appreciated. The rest of the exam went well. After paying, I walked out of the office. INTO THE SUN, WITHOUT SUNGLASSES - NEITHER THE DORKY WRAPAROUND ONES, OR A WARNING TO WEAR MY OWN. Luckily I remembered, OH SHOOT, I need sunglasses after dilation to protect my eyes. I hobbled to the car and found an old pair in there. YIKES. Overall, the office got the job done, but the dilation upsell/experience left something to be desired.< /review><GmapID>0x80deaaf75ccf31ed:0x2ad89ee5d85615ae< /GmapID>< response>

I am not a vain person by nature.  I am however concerned with my overall health and this is why I selected and have used the health and diagnostic services of Dr. Goldsmid and Dr. Langford of Arena Eyeworks.

<time>1622836809007<//time><rating>1</rating><Review>The billing practices by this office is trash and sketchy at best. I had a new patient well woman exam with Dr. Gentry in April. Keep in mind, I am very familiar with how billing for preventive care works, as I have worked for one of my insurers and I have great coverage, so this should have been a simple first appointment.

Before my appointment, patients are required to fill out a medical history form online. I should have known my visit wouldn't be billed accurately, because upon entering the exam room and having not even seen the doctor yet, the nurse or medical assistant is asking about if I had a physical in the past 12 months because this visit could be billed as an office visit. I quickly informed her that I do this every year and my appointment should be covered at 100%. Also, it's highly unprofessional to discuss/assume what a visit will be billed as/outcomes without even seeing the doctor first. If they want to know, ask when scheduling the appointment.

Upon Dr. Gentry entering the room, she noticed that I filled out a line on my medical history incorrectly. We then discussed my medical history. If part of her practice is not care about patient history when seeing new patients for the first time, then don't bother to ask. I could have scheduled another appointment about my medical history. I did not ask for a referral, yet she gave me one for a specialist.

What other issues? ... my medical history? I have never been billed for discussing my relevant medical history with a doctor. If Dr. Gentry simply wants to do exams with new patients instead of at least becoming familiar with their history, then I wouldn't recommend her at all. Just do exams and let patients go about their way.

Being new to the Bay Area, and already having limited access to great African-American providers who are also specialists, this entire experience with my first provider here was disappointing to say the least. <user>107300793860511864419<//user><Name>Teri Charles</Name><date>1519778730016< /date><Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Dr Gentry saved my life!!!!!!

About 4 years ago I was diagnosed with severe bleeding (fibroid tumors).  I had seen three other Drs in an effort to be treated. My bleeding resulted in severe anemia.  Two primary care Drs and a naturapathic Dr all confirmed my bleeding was at near grave levels.

First a very popular in network facility tried multiple times to complete the imaging; however, they had long waits for appointments and when I arrived (full of water) I had to wait for long periods in the lobby until I could no longer hold the water and was forced to reschedule.

Next, an out of network facility thought they could help by completing the imaging for the diagnosis.  They reviewed my insurance and made the appointment; but when I arrived (full of water) - they stated they could not accept my HMO insurance and turned me away.

I was then referred to Dr Gentry by a dear friend - Dr Gentry was the only complete facility that was able to complete my diagnosis and perform my surgery before "the lights went out" for me.  Dr Gentry's lab staff were patient and persistent.

Dr Gentry quickly arranged for her lab to get me an appointment. Her lab allowed me stay as long as it took to get the imaging done.  If I could no longer hold the water; then I was allowed to relieve myself and drink more water until we got the imaging done.  Dr Gentry did not allow her lab to send me away until the imaging was done and she completed the diagnosis and surgery.
